PCR was carried out to verify the 212-nt indel in the <i>Y</i> candidate gene (DCAR_032551) (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.3565#MOESM299">Supplementary Fig. 42</a>).</p><p>Expression values were log<sub>2</sub> transformed, and the WGCNA package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 127" title="Langfelder, P. &amp; Horvath, S. WGCNA: an R package for weighted correlation network analysis. BMC Bioinformatics 9, 559 (2008)." href="/articles/ng.3565#ref-CR127" id="ref-link-section-d2836e3535">127</a></sup> in R with signed correlations was used to determine gene coexpression modules with a soft threshold value <i>β</i> of 10 and a treecut value of 0.6. Functional annotation of genes within this module was determined by BLASTP search of protein sequences within this module against the <i>A. thaliana</i> TAIR10 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 128" title="Lamesch, P. et al. The Arabidopsis Information Resource (TAIR): improved gene annotation and new tools. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, D1202–D1210 (2012)." href="/articles/ng.3565#ref-CR128" id="ref-link-section-d2836e3544">128</a>) predictions, and GO enrichment analysis based on BLASTP best hits to TAIR10 was performed using AgriGO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 129" title="Du, Z., Zhou, X., Ling, Y., Zhang, Z. &amp; Su, Z. agriGO: a GO analysis toolkit for the agricultural community. Nucleic Acids Res. 38, W64–W70 (2010)." href="/articles/ng.3565#ref-CR129" id="ref-link-section-d2836e3549">129</a></sup> and PANTHER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 130" title="Mi, H., Muruganujan, A. &amp; Thomas, P.D. PANTHER in 2013: modeling the evolution of gene function, and other gene attributes, in the context of phylogenetic trees. Nucleic Acids Res. 41, D377–D386 (2013)." href="/articles/ng.3565#ref-CR130" id="ref-link-section-d2836e3553">130</a></sup>.</p><p>Genes that were simultaneously upregulated or downregulated in both yellow and dark orange samples, relative to the white and pale orange samples, were manually annotated. GO annotations and subcellular localization are also reported.</p><p>See the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.3565#MOESM295">Supplementary Note</a> for additional details.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Identification of flavonoid and isoprenoid pathway genes.</h3><p>The peptide sequences for carrot predicted genes were aligned against annotated flavonoid and isoprenoid pathway genes in the KEGG database (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.3565#MOESM300">Supplementary Tables 46, 84, and 85</a>). BLASTP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Voorrips, R.E. MapChart: software for the graphical presentation of linkage maps and QTLs. J. Hered. 93, 77–78 (2002)." href="/articles/ng.3565#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d2836e3578">69</a></sup> was carried out using default parameters. Sequences with &lt;50% identity, &lt;50 residues were excluded. Peptide sequences from genomes having orthologous relationships with retained carrot genes were extracted from the genome evolution analysis. Genes annotated from the <i>A. thaliana</i> and tomato genomes were manually verified. Multiple-sequence alignments were generated with Clustal W<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 118" title="Larkin, M.A. et al. Clustal W and Clustal X version 2.0. Bioinformatics 23, 2947–2948 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.3565#ref-CR118" id="ref-link-section-d2836e3585">118</a></sup>. Phylogenetic analyses were carried out using MEGA6 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Tamura, K., Stecher, G., Peterson, D., Filipski, A. &amp; Kumar, S. MEGA6: Molecular Evolutionary Genetics Analysis version 6.0. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 2725–2729 (2013)." href="/articles/ng.3565#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d2836e3588">84</a>) (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.3565#MOESM299">Supplementary Figs. 43</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.3565#MOESM299">44</a>). Carrot peptide sequences annotated as InterProScan IDs IPR001906 and IPR005630 and containing the N-terminal domains PF011397 and PF03936 (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.3565#MOESM300">Supplementary Table 47</a>) along with known terpene synthases (TPSs) from seven other species were used for analysis with MEGA. The amino acid substitution models tested were WAG, mtREV, Dayhoff, JTT, VT, Blosum62, and CpREV. The tree with the highest AICc value was obtained with the JTT+F model with estimation of the gamma distribution. The phylogenetic tree was then rooted at the split between the type I (TPS-c, TPS-e, TPS-f, and TPS-h) and type III (TPS-a, TPS-b, and TPS-g) subfamilies (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.3565#MOESM299">Supplementary Fig. 45</a>).</p><p>See the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.3565#MOESM295">Supplementary Note</a> for additional details.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">Accession codes.</h3><p>The genome assembly has been deposited at GenBank under accession <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=LNRQ00000000">LNRQ00000000</a> and at Phytozome. The version described in this paper is version LNRQ01000000. All raw reads have been deposited in the Sequence Read Archive (SRA) under umbrella project <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJNA285926">PRJNA285926</a>, accessions <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRP062070">SRP062070</a>, <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRP062113">SRP062113</a>, and <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=SRP062159">SRP062159</a>. Further information is available through our website (see <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="section anchor" href="/articles/ng.3565#Sec24">URLs</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec24">URLs.</h3><p>Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations (FAO) Statistics, <a href="http://faostat3.fao.org/">http://faostat3.fao.org/</a>; SOAPaligner, <a href="http://soap.genomics.org.cn/soapaligner.html">http://soap.genomics.org.cn/soapaligner.html</a>; bb.tassel, <a href="https://github.com/dsenalik/bb">https://github.com/dsenalik/bb</a>; CheckMatrix, <a href="http://www.atgc.org/XLinkage">http://www.atgc.org/XLinkage</a>; cp1 and cp2 scripts, <a href="http://www.ars.usda.gov/pandp/Docs.htm?docid=25732">http://www.ars.usda.gov/pandp/Docs.htm?docid=25732</a>; RepeatMasker and RepeatModeler, <a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/</a>; Picard tools, <a href="http://broadinstitute.github.io/picard/">http://broadinstitute.github.io/picard/</a>; TargetP web-based predictor, <a href="http://www.cbs.dtu.dk/services/TargetP/">http://www.cbs.dtu.dk/services/TargetP/</a>; <i>Arabidopsis</i> database, <a href="https://www.arabidopsis.org/Blast/index.jsp">https://www.arabidopsis.org/Blast/index.jsp</a>. Information from this publication is available at <a href="http://www.ars.usda.gov/pandp/Docs.htm?docid=25732">http://www.ars.usda.gov/pandp/Docs.htm?docid=25732</a>.</p></div></div></section>

Iovene, A.M.-P., E.M., E.G., and D.G. performed evaluation and analysis of repetitive elements and <i>in situ</i> hybridization. M. Iorizzo, D. Senalik, P.Z., and S.C. performed evolution analysis. Iorizzo, S.E., D. Senalik, M.B., and D. Spooner performed the resequencing analysis. M. Iorizzo, S.E., P. Satapoomin, and P. Simon performed the carotenoid accumulation analysis. M. Iorizzo, S.E., D. Senalik, P.Z., P. Satapoomin, M.B., M. Iovene, A.M.-P., E.G., D.G., D. Spooner, A.V.D., and P. Simon wrote the paper. M. Iorizzo and P. Simon organized the manuscript. A.V.D. and P.               <p class="c-article-further-reading__journal-title" id="journal-name-3">
